<UserId.>109805023620756977762<//UserId.><Rating>1< /Rating><time>1505606636195< /time>< Text>
Horrible Construction/Renovtion Disaster!!

I moved in 4 months ago and this has been going on for 3 months. It's 6 days a week of noise and 7 days a week of inconvenience, unsightly equipment, multiple dumpsters, materials, trash, construction vehicles and debris. My parking is in the other half of the complex, across the street, so I've been dealing with the mess since the beginning of the demo in June.

For over a month, the gym was closed, the common "oceanview patio with free wifi" was covered in junk, the common rec room was closed, and even the office was closed. They haven't used their app even once to broadcast messages to tenants. The grounds have been a disaster since mid-June -- as if they're not even going to pretend to keep up appearances.

In July, I stopped going down to look at the ocean, because they were ripping apart the buildings facing the ocean and it was just too depressing to see the mess everywhere. (PS - they said they were going to restore beach access that was washed out earlier in the year, but I'm not holding my breath. Google Maps still shows the path, but it's gone. Also the Oceanaire property map shows an ocean path, which is not there.)

They haven't done anything to contain the  work to a particular section of the property and complete one building before beginning demo on an adjacent building. Instead they work on another building on the opposite end. They are randomly criss-crossing lengthwise across the property (south-north) instead of working east-west). The way they're doing it, it's as if they're purposely trying to MAXIMIZE the  inconvenience of everyone and make it so that nothing looks pretty or peaceful or at all like home.

I was only given 6 days notice on 9/1 to clear my patio before 9/8 and to keep my windows closed for 2 months for renovation to my building. I had purchased $300 of patio furniture and plants when I moved here, not knowing that they were planning a major renovation and everything would all have to be stored inside.  4 days into my apartment renovation, the wrecking crew cut an electrical line to my kitchen and my refrigerator was without power for about 30 hours (and I'll have to toss everything). In the response to my online Maintenance request early that evening 9/12, a technician showed up at my door at 11:45 pm(!) and left at 12:45 am(!) without any resolution. The 2nd day they brought an extension cord. The 3rd day an electrician came to repair it and left the fridge hooked up to the extension cord and left a mess. The 4th day they came back to plug the fridge in properly and remove the extension cord (because I complained) and they still left the mess on the countertop, plus white handprints on my black fridge and countertop.  My 2nd story balcony was left completely exposed on 1 side for 3 days before they boarded it up. The front porch lights have been ripped off for 3 daya now and it's difficult to watch for hazards at night, especially because they leave junk everywhere in the walkways.

There has been no offer to reduce the rent and I've contacted a lawyer.

< text>
I've been at OceanAire longer than most; four years in November. Over the years the community has had its ups & downs - most noticeably when it underwent major construction for about a year (which drove many of the negative reviews online). They've made some great positive changes since then, most notably in management of the community. This remains a really nice place to live - quiet, comfortable, and with an ideal location right on the ocean. The staff are terrific. They are highly responsive and the maintenance team is the best (particular shoutouts to Mike, Zee, and Omar).
With that said, lately I've been disappointed with the amenities that OceanAire promotes front & center on their website as a value-add to residents. That lovely spa that you see on the home page? Hasn't worked for months; basically all summer. The fitness center? Machines are frequently broken or not properly maintained, and bizarrely there is a personal trainer running her business out of it all day which monopolizes the equipment. Be careful investing too much value in the beach access, because this part of the coastline experiences major erosion, which means restoration efforts need to happen which block or disrupt that access. (The access was closed for over a year when a sinkhole took out a chunk of the path, and as of the time of writing this review the beach is a major construction site due to a necessary rebuild of the seawall.)
Overall, I still recommend OceanAire to prospective tenants, but please make your decision based solely on the apartment itself, and not in the peripheral amenities which have become unreliable and consequently far less valuable.</text>

Upon terminating my contract, a snag came up regarding term and dates, which Michael efficiently resolved with no complications.  Thankfully, nothing cast a shadow on a perfect summer stay.
Thanks Crew!
P.S.  Ask Zee for tips on hiking and biking trails in the area.< /review>

<Time>1569618429388<//Time><Rating>3< /Rating><Review>I've been at OceanAire longer than most; four years in November. Over the years the community has had its ups & downs - most noticeably when it underwent major construction for about a year (which drove many of the negative reviews online). They've made some great positive changes since then, most notably in management of the community. This remains a really nice place to live - quiet, comfortable, and with an ideal location right on the ocean. The staff are terrific. They are highly responsive and the maintenance team is the best (particular shoutouts to Mike, Zee, and Omar).
With that said, lately I've been disappointed with the amenities that OceanAire promotes front & center on their website as a value-add to residents. That lovely spa that you see on the home page? Hasn't worked for months; basically all summer. The fitness center? Machines are frequently broken or not properly maintained, and bizarrely there is a personal trainer running her business out of it all day which monopolizes the equipment. Be careful investing too much value in the beach access, because this part of the coastline experiences major erosion, which means restoration efforts need to happen which block or disrupt that access. (The access was closed for over a year when a sinkhole took out a chunk of the path, and as of the time of writing this review the beach is a major construction site due to a necessary rebuild of the seawall.)

< review>
I've lived here for 2+ years and used to sing praises of the place. I was told that the same management company was kept on after the property was sold and renamed from LandsEnd to OceanAire. However, with all that's going on it's surprising how poorly everything is being handled. As a side note, the beach access - one of the reasons we chose to live here has not been fixed for almost a year now.

CONSTRUCTION: So far, it's been a very poor experience. There's dust, noise, and construction items everywhere. We were given 3 days notice to move all of our patio furniture off during construction with no place to put it all. We were told that, for our specific building, it would be worked on for 2 months and to "keep your curtains drawn to ensure privacy.  Crews will be working at the windows and on balconies with visual access to your home." It's odd that they wouldn't finish 1 building at a time. Much of the parking (including street parking) has been taken over by construction vehicles and building materials. Multiple times, they've also had people enter our apartment for cabling related to the construction. We are given notice, but in reality, what choice do we have if we are not home and prefer that people do not enter? Today is supposed to be the final day of construction; however, the painting is still in progress. It's not going to complete within the deadline they've informed us of.

OFFICE MANAGEMENT: They will make no reasonable accommodations for any of the inconveniences, have no power to do so, and will not point you to people that can help. Our rent continues to increase. Our keys do not work for community shared spaces, and we were told by other apartment renters that we have to get our keys reprogrammed. There's a couple of stoic and rude office staff (with an exception or 2). You eventually give up since it's uncomfortable to list concerns to people that don't care and cannot help.

We still currently live in the complex due to the community of friends that have moved here with us. All 8 of which, not surprisingly, have had their own unhappy apartment issues. My hope is that the management company or owners really take into account what our community members are saying and make an effort to reasonably accommodate for issues. Currently, it just feels like existing apartment renters are being punished for staying here, try to voice concerns, but are faced with stoicism and an "unfortunately, it is what it is" attitude.<//review>

< review>
Before it changed its name and owner, this place was called Land's End Apartment Homes. Back then, it was a great place to live under the management of Joe and Shelley. After they left, the management team kept changing every few months. I even stopped by the office today and learned the team has been overhauled again(4th time in 6 months). Needless to say, this high turnover rate has made getting anything done impossible. Communication has been terrible as well. The bigger issue may be that they found a sinkhole 100 feet from the property, making it dangerous and blocking access to the beach, which is the essentially the best amenity at this place. With all these unexpected and unpleasant changes, I made the decision to move out.
After reading some of the other reviews, I'm noticing people are saying that the walls and floors are really thin here. Having lived only on the top floor units, I can't really relate to that. One thing that does get loud are the in-unit laundry machines. They are incredibly loud.

UPDATE(11/01/2017): I just read the response from the owner and the suggestion that they "have been in constant communication" with me is not authentic. I was never contacted about it. Ultimately, I posted my review after I moved out so there was nothing to be done. That said, I have been told that there is a new management team and new updates to the units taking place, so I can't speak for current state of the apartments here.

UPDATE(03/01/2018): I have been contacted by a number of current residents asking if I'd be willing to provide information on incidents where the management was dishonest about the state of apartments and facilities, possibly to take action legally. It seems even the current residents are experiencing lingering issues with the management team. Disappointed to hear that things have continued to deteriorate at this place.</review>

< review>
Lands End is an amazing place to live!  We lived there for about 9 months and had to move for a job out of state.  The view is unbelievable and nearly all year round you can see whales, dolphins, sea lions, pelicans & more right from your apartment!  The only issues we had were that the garbage disposal broke, the fridge was shutting off and on & the dryer wasn't drying very well, but they resolved all of the issues quickly.  Some reviews complained about the washer/dryer combination machine not drying well, but the filter has to be cleaned every few months, so simply put in a work order and the dryer will work great after being cleaned.  The complex itself is a little older and we can often hear our neighbors upstairs, but we would definitely continue to live here if we were staying in Pacifica.  It is clean, safe and very peaceful.  It is very close to Safeway, good restaurants and Hwy 1.  It was also nice to have a gym, jacuzzi & clubhouse that I could walk to in less than a minute.  The price for the SF Bay Area is reasonable; you will pay about what you'd pay in many other apt. complexes in the area but this one is right on the ocean!  But nothing's perfect...you will not get all of your security deposit back; you will have to pay for carpet shampooing, repainting, apartment cleaning, etc. when you move out.</review>

<Date>1534182332427<//Date><Rate>1<//Rate><review>The good:
1) The location is absolutely incredible. We saw whales, seals and dolphins frequently and got to go down to the beach every day. My fiancé and I as well as our dog loved that very much. Pacifica is such an awesome town in the bay that isn’t too far from the city.
2) Office staff is friendly.

The bad: phew...here it goes...
1) They will squeeze every penny out of your security deposit possible. There was one ding in our wall, about 3/4 inch in diameter and we got charged $150 for painting. We also spent the entire day cleaning and shampooing the carpets before we moved. The place looked pristine, yet we still got hit with a $150 charge for apartment cleaning and $95 for carpet cleaning. I’m sure Trinity will respond with a justification for this, however it was an unethical move regardless...as our apartment was beyond acceptable for the next resident’s move in.
2) Mice! You’ll be charged monthly for pest control, yet the pests are far from controlled around Oceanaire. We saw mice as well as their feces in and around our apartment frequently.
3) Very long response times to maintenance requests. Expect about a week min to get something scheduled (not completed, scheduled). I also informed the office about a cable being broken on the smith machine in the community gym. They did nothing for 3 weeks, then their next action was to put an out of order sign on it that says “we apologize for any inconvenience this may have caused” rather than fixing the broken equipment. I’d estimate that 50-75% of the emails that come from the office end with that same note...”we apologize for any inconvenience this may have caused” rather than addressing the root cause of the issues on hand. Proactive VS reactive management. Last, the emergency maintenance line was non-functioning both times I needed it which was brought to management’s attention. I am not sure if that has been resolved, but it doesn’t change the fact that it happened.
4) Electricity issues. If you use two things simultaneously that draw a lot of power, expect a short. We couldn’t use the following things at the same time: microwave, hairdryer, toaster, washer/dryer. Simply very old electrical wiring throughout property.
5) Many of the apartments will likely be at the bottom of the cliff within the next 5 years, less if the impending earthquake hits. The sea cliff erosion at this location is a real threat.< /review>< Pics>

<Text>If you would have asked me this time last year if I had ever utilized or had any intention of visiting a pawn shop I would have looked at you and laughed and said absolutely not! However as luck would have it life happened and the entire dynamic of my world shifted leaving me in a position needing to visit local pawn shops in order to financially take care of my family! After a horrendous experience "Best Collatera" (definitely not the best) where I was made to feel stupid my items were devalued and I was embarrassed walking out crying I stumbled across Granters pawn shop in Vallejo! I can wholeheartedly say if you are having a difficult time or if you have the same perception of pawn shops that I had up until about six months ago I couldn't recommend granters more if I tried! Everyone that works there is knowledgeable friendly compassionate and I genuinely feel wants to be of assistance! I don't know anyone that is excited at the idea of having to pawn items dear to them for a loan, but I will say going to granters is like walking in and seeing a bunch of your friends! <text>Found myself in a tight spot financially,  it happens...right?  Had been across town to Granters competition an hour before trying to get a loan using my baby as Collateral....Best idea I could think of.  NO....not my girl, come on, man!
My actual baby...a gloss black Fender Professional Telecaster Shawbucker with a maple neck.  I would give my left nut to keep my baby in the crib.  But the landlord ain't interested in my left OR right.  So I needed some blues.  I had borrowed against my Gibson Custom Shop Les Paul at the competition last week but now I bring baby to them and they said, " We can only loan $100 on that guitar." I knew right away these cats DO NOT KNOW GUITARS.  Look, they might be Best on some Collateral decisions, but they were out of tune with my baby.
The guy helping me said, " Uh, yeah man we can only sell this for $300 if you don't come back for it."  I gave him my card and said "EVERYTIME you get a fiddle in and BEFORE you put it out on the sales floor PLEASE give me a call. Because you have NO IDEA WHAT YOU ARE DOING" I wonder how many Fender Professional Telecasters this cat has hung $300 price tags on.
Needless to say I grabbed my baby's neck and whispered softly in her Shawbuckers, "Let's go baby...we are not being treated with respect here." My baby cried out on her G string...."GRANTERS...Daddy!!!"
So we head to the East side of Vallejo and the 2 guys there KNEW THEIR GAME!!!
I told him, "Hey brother, I'm in a tight spot, can you please help me with a loan? My baby can stay with you guys as collateral." They said, "what will get you out of the hole? These guys are top shelf. Good business-minded, friendly, and knowledgeable lenders that understand there is more to collateral than just a name.

What a wonderful little find! Upon our arrival to San Diego, we made our regular pilgrimage to our favorite spot. Much to our dismay, it was closed but that was short lived as we discovered Los Panchos. I had the beef taco & cheese enchilada combo. My husband had a steak tostada salad, and our son had the beef taquitos with a side of beans. The chips and salsa flowed while we waited. My husband and I loved our lunch. My son didn't care for the beef taquitos as they were ground beef with potato... not at all what he expected. But he loved the beans and made that his meal with chips. We will definitely be back next time in SD!</review>

<Time>1579427909504< /Time><rate>5< /rate>< text>
This new spot for Panchos was long overdue. They did a great job conceptually. I really enjoy that it still has fast food service but in an upscale environment.

They added a "Cantina" area which has a nice patio that overlooks 5th Avenue. It is at a major intersection so it is not super quiet or romantic but it is fun. The drinks are great and the service is on point.

I, personally do not like the chairs in the main dining area that have the legs that kind of fan out as I did trip over them going back to my seat after getting a soda refill.

The counter staff was very knowledgeable and in tune with the menu. Clearly occupying a space that large they cant be 24 hours like their last location next door which is now occupied by Dunkin'. It would be cool if they were still 24 but maybe had only some of the venue open late night.
That is just me being a hungry guy at 3 am.<//text>

< text>
I was skeptical when I heard Los Panchos took over the corner, but after one visit I'm a believer. Half taco shop, half cantina, this is Los Panchos Hillcrest done right.  Not only can you walk in and take out solid taqueria style Mexican food (as fast, inexpensive and delicious as any of the city's many Los Panchos locations), you can also have a seat at the full bar, or inside watching one of several large TVs, or outside on the patio enjoying the passerbys. I recommend enjoying the awesome happy hour which offers several drinks and food options (until 7pm!). It's no frills, So Cal style Mexican and margaritas at their very best and right in the heart of Hillcrest!< /text>
